Outline

Edit and raw actions

|     |     |
| --- | --- |
| title | Profanity |
| description | The Profanity plugin will scan your codebase for profanity in places like comments, constants and properties |

Profanity
=========

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/profanity.md#profanity)

**Source code**: [github.com/pestphp/pest-plugin-profanity](https://github.com/pestphp/pest-plugin-profanity)

The Profanity plugin will scan your codebase for profanity in places like comments, constants and properties. This can help you maintain a more professional and respectful codebase. As developers, we've all faced moments of frustration, whether it be debugging a persistent issue or trying to decipher confusing code written by someone else. These moments can sometimes result in the inclusion of profanity in your code.

To start using Pest's Profanity plugin, you need to require the plugin via Composer.

```shell
composer require pestphp/pest-plugin-profanity --dev
```

After requiring the plugin, you may utilize the `--profanity` option to generate a report of your profanity.

```shell
./vendor/bin/pest --profanity
```

Profanity does not require you to write any tests. Instead, it analyses your codebase and generates a report of your profanity. This report will display a list of files and their corresponding profanity results.

[![](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/raw/4.x/assets/img/profanity.png)](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/assets/img/profanity.png)

If any of your files contain profanity, they will be highlighted in red and displayed using their respective line numbers and the profane word(s) that have been found.

As an example, `pr31(fuck)` means that the word "fuck" was found on line 31.

Specific Language
-----------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/profanity.md#specific-language)

Often, a codebase is a single language, so you would only want to flag profanity for the language of the codebase. To do this, you can use the `--language` option:

```shell
./vendor/bin/pest --profanity --language=en
```

If needed, you can pass in multiple comma separated languages too:

```shell
./vendor/bin/pest --profanity --language=en,da
```

We currently support: `ar`, `da`, `en`, `es`, `it`, `ja`, `nl`, `pt_BR` and `ru`. If no language is specified, we use `en` as the default.

Include Words
-------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/profanity.md#include-words)

There may be times when you want to flag certain words specific to your application as profane. To do this, you can use the `--include` option:

```shell
./vendor/bin/pest --profanity --include=elephpant
```

Exclude Words
-------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/profanity.md#exclude-words)

There may be times when you want to exclude certain words from being flagged up as profane. To do this, you can use the `--exclude` option:

```shell
./vendor/bin/pest --profanity --exclude=elephpant
```

Compact Output
--------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/profanity.md#compact-output)

Often, when checking for profanity, you only want to see files that do contain profanity. To do this, you can use the `--compact` option:

```shell
./vendor/bin/pest --profanity --compact
```

Different Formats
-----------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/profanity.md#different-formats)

In addition, Pest supports reporting the profanity results to a specific file:

```shell
./vendor/bin/pest --profanity --output=my-report.json
```

Exclude Lines
-------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/profanity.md#exclude-lines)

If you wish to exclude certain lines that contain profanity from being flagged, without excluding words from the whole application, you can tell the checker to ignore certain lines:

```html
const string Fuck; // @pest-ignore-profanity
```

* * *

In this chapter, we have discussed Pest's Profanity plugin and how it can be used to help you maintain a professional codebase. In the following chapter, we will explore additional CLI options that Pest provides: [CLI API Reference](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/docs/cli-api-reference)

You can’t perform that action at this time.

---

|     |     |
| --- | --- |
| title | Plugins |
| description | In this section, we will discuss the official and community developed plugins that we endorse. Plugins primarily offer namespaced functions, console commands, custom expectations, and additional command-line options to augment the default Pest experience. |

Plugins
=======

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/plugins.md#plugins)

In this section, we will discuss the official and community developed plugins that we endorse. Plugins primarily offer namespaced functions, console commands, custom expectations, and additional command-line options to augment the default Pest experience.

If you are a plugin developer, please consult our [documentation on creating plugins](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/docs/creating-plugins)
 for more information on how to create Pest plugins.

The following plugins are maintained by the Pest team:

*   [Faker](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/plugins.md#faker)
    
*   [Laravel](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/plugins.md#laravel)
    
*   [Livewire](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/plugins.md#livewire)
    

* * *

Faker
-----

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/plugins.md#faker)

**Source code**: [github.com/pestphp/pest-plugin-faker](https://github.com/pestphp/pest-plugin-faker)

To start using Pest's Faker plugin, you need to require the plugin via Composer.

```shell
composer require pestphp/pest-plugin-faker --dev
```

After installing the plugin, you may utilize the namespaced `fake` function to generate fake data for your tests.

```html
use function Pest\Faker\fake;

it('generates a name', function () {
    $name = fake()->name; // random name...

    //
});
```

You can also designate the "locale" that should be utilized by the `fake()` function by providing the locale to the function.

```html
use function Pest\Faker\fake;

it('generates a portuguese name', function () {
    $name = fake('pt_PT')->name; // Nuno Maduro

    //
});
```

To learn more about Faker, including comprehensive details about the API it provides, please consult [its official documentation](https://fakerphp.github.io/)
.

* * *

Laravel
-------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/plugins.md#laravel)

**Source code**: [github.com/pestphp/pest-plugin-laravel](https://github.com/pestphp/pest-plugin-laravel)

To start using Pest's Laravel plugin, you need to require this plugin via Composer.

```shell
composer require pestphp/pest-plugin-laravel --dev
```

This plugin adds additional Artisan commands and functions to the default Pest installation. For example, to generate a new test in the `tests/Feature` directory, you can now utilize the `pest:test` Artisan command.

```shell
php artisan pest:test UsersTest
```

You may provide the `--unit` option when creating a test to place the test in the `tests/Unit` directory.

```shell
php artisan pest:test UsersTest --unit
```

Executing the `pest:dataset` Artisan command will create a fresh dataset in the `tests/Datasets` directory.

```shell
php artisan pest:dataset Emails
```

As you may know, Laravel provides a variety of assertions you can take advantage of in your feature tests. When using Pest's Laravel plugin, you may access all of those assertions as you typically would.

```html
it('has a welcome page', function () {
    $this->get('/')->assertStatus(200);
});
```

In addition, with the assistance of this plugin, it is possible for you to bypass the `$this` variable while using namespaced functions such as `actingAs`, `get`, `post` and `delete`.

```html
use function Pest\Laravel\{get};

it('has a welcome page', function () {
    get('/')->assertStatus(200);
    // same as $this->get('/')...
});
```

To illustrate this convenient feature using another example, we can write a test acting as an authenticated user accessing the restricted dashboard page.

```html
use App\Models\User;
use function Pest\Laravel\{actingAs};

test('authenticated user can access the dashboard', function () {
    $user = User::factory()->create();

    actingAs($user)->get('/dashboard')
        ->assertStatus(200);
});
```

As you may expect, all of the assertions that were previously accessible via `$this->` are available as namespace functions.

```html
use function Pest\Laravel\{actingAs, get, post, delete, ...};
```

You can find the full testing documentation on the Laravel website: [laravel.com/docs/12.x/testing](https://laravel.com/docs/12.x/testing)
.

* * *

Livewire
--------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/plugins.md#livewire)

**Source code**: [github.com/pestphp/pest-plugin-livewire](https://github.com/pestphp/pest-plugin-livewire)

To install Pest's Livewire plugin, you need to require the plugin via Composer.

```shell
composer require pestphp/pest-plugin-livewire --dev
```

After installing the plugin, you may use the `livewire` namespaced function to access your Livewire components.

```html
use function Pest\Livewire\livewire;

it('can be incremented', function () {
    livewire(Counter::class)
        ->call('increment')
        ->assertSee(1);
});

it('can be decremented', function () {
    livewire(Counter::class)
        ->call('decrement')
        ->assertSee(-1);
});
```

* * *

In this section, we have seen how plugins can enhance your Pest experience. Now, let's see how you can manage your team's tasks and responsibilities using Pest: [Team Management](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/docs/team-management)

You can’t perform that action at this time.

---

*   Preview
    
*   Code
    
*   Blame

|     |     |
| --- | --- |
| title | Skipping Tests |
| description | During the development process, there may be times when you need to temporarily disable a test. Rather than commenting out the code, we recommended using the \`skip()\` method. |

Skipping Tests
==============

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/skipping-tests.md#skipping-tests)

During the development process, there may be times when you need to temporarily disable a test. Rather than commenting out the code, we recommended using the `skip()` method.

```html
it('has home', function () {
    //
})->skip();
```

When running your tests, Pest will inform you about any tests that were skipped.

[![](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/raw/4.x/assets/img/skip.webp?1)](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/assets/img/skip.webp?1)

You may also provide the reason for skipping the test, which Pest will display when running your tests.

```html
it('has home', function () {
    //
})->skip('temporarily unavailable');
```

In addition, there may be times when you want to skip a test based on a given condition. In these cases, you may provide a boolean value as the first argument to the `skip()` method. This test will only be skipped if the boolean value evaluates to `true`.

```html
it('has home', function () {
    //
})->skip($condition == true, 'temporarily unavailable');
```

You may pass a closure as the first argument to the `skip()` method to defer the evaluation of the condition until the `beforeEach()` hook of your test case has been executed.

```html
it('has home', function () {
    //
})->skip(fn () => DB::getDriverName() !== 'mysql', 'db driver not supported');
```

You may also skip tests based on the environment in which they are running using the `skipLocally()` or `skipOnCi()` methods.

```html
it('has home', function () {
    //
})->skipLocally(); // or skipOnCi()
```

To skip a test on a particular operating system, you can make use of the `skipOnWindows()`, `skipOnMac()`, or `skipOnLinux()`.

```html
it('has home', function () {
    //
})->skipOnWindows(); // or skipOnMac() or skipOnLinux() ...
```

Alternatively, you can skip a test on all operating systems except one by using `onlyOnWindows()`, `onlyOnMac()`, or `onlyOnLinux()`.

```html
it('has home', function() {
    //
})->onlyOnWindows(); // or onlyOnMac() or onlyOnLinux() ...
```

Sometimes, you may want to skip a test on a specific PHP version. In these cases, you may use the `skipOnPhp()` method.

```html
it('has home', function () {
    //
})->skipOnPhp('>=8.0.0');
```

The valid operators for the `skipOnPhp()` method are `>`, `>=`, `<`, and `<=`.

Finally, you may even invoke the `skip()` method within your `beforeEach()` hook to conveniently skip an entire test file.

```html
beforeEach()->skip(); // or skipOnCi(), etc...
```

Creating todos
--------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/skipping-tests.md#creating-todos)

You might want to add a couple of empty tests to make sure you don't forget to add them later. The `todo()` can be useful in this situation.

```html
it('has home', function () {
    //
})->todo();
```

* * *

As your codebase expands, it's advisable to consider enhancing the speed of your test suite. To assist you with that, we offer comprehensive documentation on optimizing your test suite: [Optimizing Tests](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/docs/optimizing-tests)

You can’t perform that action at this time.

---

|     |     |
| --- | --- |
| title | Type Coverage |
| description | Type Coverage is a metric used to measure the percentage of code that is covered by type declarations |

Type Coverage
=============

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/type-coverage.md#type-coverage)

**Source code**: [github.com/pestphp/pest-plugin-type-coverage](https://github.com/pestphp/pest-plugin-type-coverage)

Type Coverage is a metric used to measure the percentage of code that is covered by type declarations. This can help developers identify parts of their code that may not be fully typed, indicating a potential risk for bugs and other issues.

To start using Pest's Type Coverage plugin, you need to require the plugin via Composer.

```shell
composer require pestphp/pest-plugin-type-coverage --dev
```

After requiring the plugin, you may utilize the `--type-coverage` option to generate a report of your type coverage.

```shell
./vendor/bin/pest --type-coverage
```

Unlike code coverage, type coverage does not require you to write any tests. Instead, it analyzes your codebase and generates a report of your type coverage. This report will display a list of files and their corresponding type coverage results.

[![](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/raw/4.x/assets/img/type-coverage.png)](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/assets/img/type-coverage.png)

If any of your files are missing type declarations, they will be highlighted in yellow and displayed using their respective line numbers, and type of declaration that is missing.

As example, `rt31` means that the return type of the function on line 31 is missing. On the other hand, `pa31` means that the parameter type of the function on line 31 is missing.

Ignoring Errors
---------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/type-coverage.md#ignoring-errors)

Sometimes, you may want to ignore a specific error or line of code. To do so, you may use the `@pest-ignore-type` annotation:

```html
    protected $except = [ // @pest-ignore-type\
        // ...\
    ];
}
```

Compact Output
--------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/type-coverage.md#compact-output)

Often, when checking type coverage, you only want to see files that do not currently have 100% type coverage. To do this, you can use the `--compact` option:

```shell
./vendor/bin/pest --type-coverage --compact
```

Minimum Threshold Enforcement
-----------------------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/type-coverage.md#minimum-threshold-enforcement)

Just like code coverage, type coverage can also be enforced. To ensure any code that is added to your application is fully typed, you can use the `--type-coverage` and `--min` options to define the minimum threshold values for type coverage results. If the specified thresholds are not met, Pest will report a failure.

```shell
./vendor/bin/pest --type-coverage --min=100
```

Different Formats
-----------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/type-coverage.md#different-formats)

In addition, Pest supports reporting the type coverage to a specific file:

```shell
./vendor/bin/pest --type-coverage --min=100 --type-coverage-json=my-report.json
```

* * *

In this chapter, we have discussed Pest's Type Coverage plugin and how it can be used to measure the percentage of code that is covered by type declarations. In the following chapter, we explain how can you mutation testing to improve the quality of your tests: [Mutation Testing →](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/docs/mutation-testing)

You can’t perform that action at this time.

---

|     |     |
| --- | --- |
| title | Test Dependencies |
| description | Sometimes, tests require certain preconditions or events to occur prior to their execution or else they will not succeed. For example, you may only be able to verify that users are able to modify their accounts if you have first verified that an account can be established. |

Test Dependency
===============

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/test-dependencies.md#test-dependency)

Sometimes, tests require certain preconditions or events to occur prior to their execution or else they will not succeed. For example, you may only be able to verify that users are able to modify their accounts if you have first verified that an account can be established.

To address this issue, Pest offers the `depends()` method, which allows a "Child" test to specify that it depends on one or more "Parent" tests.

```html
test('parent', function () {
    expect(true)->toBeTrue();
});

test('child', function () {
    expect(false)->toBeFalse();
})->depends('parent');
```

In this example, the `child` test will be triggered once the `parent` test has successfully completed.

[![](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/raw/4.x/assets/img/depends.webp?1)](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/assets/img/depends.webp?1)

If the `parent` test fails, the `child` test will be bypassed and an informative message will be displayed in your test results.

```html
test('parent', function () {
    expect(true)->toBeFalse();
});

test('child', function () {
    expect(false)->toBeFalse();
})->depends('parent');
```

The example above results in the following output:

[![](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/raw/4.x/assets/img/depends-fail.webp?1)](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/assets/img/depends-fail.webp?1)

It is important to remember that the `it()` function prefixes the test with "it" by default. Thus, when referencing the test name via the `depends()` method, you should include the "it " prefix.

```html
it('is the parent', function () {
    expect(true)->toBeTrue();
});

test('child', function () {
    expect(false)->toBeFalse();
})->depends('it is the parent');
```

Results is:

[![](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/raw/4.x/assets/img/depends-pass.webp?1)](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/assets/img/depends-pass.webp?1)

Parent tests can even provide return values that can be accessed as arguments in the `child` test.

```html
test('parent', function () {
    expect(true)->toBeTrue();

    return 'from parent';
});

test('child', function ($parentValue) {
    var_dump($parentValue); // from parent

    expect($parentValue)->toBe('from parent');
})->depends('parent');
```

It is also possible to add multiple dependencies to a test. However, all parent tests must pass, and the values returned by each test will be available as function parameters in the same order as the specified dependencies.

```html
test('a', function () {
    expect(true)->toBeTrue();

    return 'a';
});

test('b', function () {
    expect(true)->toBeTrue();

    return 'b';
});

test('c', function () {
    expect(true)->toBeTrue();

    return 'c';
});

test('d', function ($testA, $testC, $testB) {
    var_dump($testA); // a
    var_dump($testB); // b
    var_dump($testC); // c
})->depends('a', 'b', 'c');
```

* * *

While test dependencies are uncommon, they can be useful for optimizing your tests and minimizing the need to recreate resources repeatedly. In the next chapter, we will explore how you can create plugins: [Creating Plugins](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/docs/creating-plugins)

You can’t perform that action at this time.

---

| title | Pest v4 Is Here — Now with Browser Testing |
| description | Today, we're thrilled to announce Pest v4 — our biggest release yet, featuring powerful new browser testing with parallel support and full Laravel integration. |

> To get started with Pest v4's new features including browser testing, please refer to the upgrade guide: [Upgrade Guide →](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/docs/upgrade-guide)
> .

*   [Browser Testing](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/pest-v4-is-here-now-with-browser-testing.md#content-pest-v4-is-here-now-with-browser-testing)

*   [Profanity Checking](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/pest-v4-is-here-now-with-browser-testing.md#content-profanity-checking)

Pest v4 Is Here — Now with Browser Testing
==========================================

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/pest-v4-is-here-now-with-browser-testing.md#pest-v4-is-here--now-with-browser-testing)

Today, we're thrilled to announce the release of **Pest v4**, bringing the biggest testing upgrade yet: powerful **[Browser Testing](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/docs/browser-testing)
**. Pest's new browser testing features let you run elegant, maintainable browser tests — with first-class support for Laravel's testing API and the ability to run tests in parallel. For the first time, this is browser testing that feels as good as writing unit tests.

Here is the creator of Pest, [Nuno Maduro](https://twitter.com/enunomaduro)
, demoing the new browser testing features in Pest v4 at Laracon US:

[![Pest v4](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/raw/4.x/assets/pest4_play.png)](https://youtu.be/f5gAgwwwwOI?si=LtPpySZe3tf8qMjz&t=52)

Here is an example of Browser Testing using [Laravel](https://laravel.com/)
:

```html
it('may reset the password', function () {
    // access any laravel testing helpers...
    Notification::fake();

    // access to the database — using the RefreshDatabase trait (even sqlite in memory...)
    $this->actingAs(User::factory()->create());

    $page = visit('/sign-in') // visit on a real browser...
        ->on()->mobile() // or ->desktop(), ->tablet(), etc...
        ->inDarkMode(); // or ->inLightMode()

    $page->assertSee('Sign In')
         ->click('Forgot Password?')
         ->type('email', 'nuno@laravel.com')
         ->press('Send Reset Link')
         ->assertSee('We have emailed your password reset link!')
         ->assertNoJavascriptErrors(); // or ->assertNoConsoleLogs()

    Notification::assertSent(ResetPassword::class);
});
```

With Pest v4's browser testing, you can:

*   Seamlessly use **Laravel features** like `Event::fake()`, `assertAuthenticated()`, and model factories
*   Use `RefreshDatabase`, even with SQLite in-memory databases, to ensure a clean state for each test
*   Test on **multiple browsers** (Chrome, Firefox, Safari)
*   Test on **different devices** and viewports (like iPhone 14 Pro, tablets, or custom breakpoints)
*   Switch **color schemes** (light/dark mode)
*   Interact with the page (click, type, scroll, select, submit, drag-and-drop, touch gestures, etc.)
*   Run **parallel browser tests** for dramatically faster suites
*   Take **screenshots** or pause tests for debugging
*   …all with the elegance of Pest syntax
*   **Playwright-based** — modern, fast, and reliable

To get started with browser testing in Pest, you need to install the Pest Browser Plugin:

```shell
composer require pestphp/pest-plugin-browser --dev

npm install playwright@latest
npx playwright install
```

After, you may use the `visit()` function anywhere. Finally, running this test is as simple as executing `./vendor/bin/pest` in your terminal. Pest will handle the rest, launching a browser, navigating to the page, and performing the actions you specified.

Smoke Testing
-------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/pest-v4-is-here-now-with-browser-testing.md#smoke-testing)

Smoke testing your application in real browsers has never been easier. With Pest v4, you can literally visit all your application pages, and ensure they don't throw any JavaScript errors, and they don't log any console errors.

```html
$routes = ['/', '/about', '/contact'];

visit($routes)->assertNoSmoke();

// assertNoSmoke() is a shorthand for:
// - assertNoJavascriptErrors()
// - assertNoConsoleLogs()
```

Visual Regression Testing
-------------------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/pest-v4-is-here-now-with-browser-testing.md#visual-regression-testing)

Want to ensure your pages look exactly as expected over time? Pest v4 introduces visual regression testing with the `assertScreenshotMatches()` assertion. This allows you to take screenshots of your pages and compare them against baseline images, ensuring that your UI remains consistent across changes.

```html
$pages = visit(['/', '/about', '/contact']);

$pages->assertScreenshotMatches();
```

This is just a glimpse of what Browser Testing in Pest v4 can do. Find out more about the new features below, and check out the [Browser Testing documentation](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/docs/browser-testing)
 for a complete guide on how to get started.

Test Sharding
-------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/pest-v4-is-here-now-with-browser-testing.md#test-sharding)

Pest v4 introduces **Test Sharding**, allowing you to split your test suite into smaller, manageable chunks. This is particularly useful for large applications (or when running browser tests) where running all tests at once can be time-consuming.

This feature is particularly useful on CI platforms, where on things like GitHub actions you can no longer scale vertical, but rather horizontally. This means you can run your tests in parallel across multiple machines, significantly speeding up your test suite execution.

To get started with Test Sharding, you can use the `--shard` option when running Pest:

```shell
# GitHub Workflow One
./vendor/bin/pest --shard=1/4

# GitHub Workflow Two
./vendor/bin/pest --shard=2/4

# GitHub Workflow Three
./vendor/bin/pest --shard=3/4

# GitHub Workflow Four
./vendor/bin/pest --shard=4/4
```

You may combine this with the `--parallel` option to run your tests in parallel, and this way trully maximize your test suite execution speed:

```shell
./vendor/bin/pest --shard=1/4 --parallel
```

Finally, to easily set up sharding your CI configuration, you just have to ensure each job in your CI configuration runs a different shard of your test suite. For example, in GitHub Actions, you can use the `matrix` strategy to define multiple jobs that run different shards:

```yaml
strategy:
  matrix:
    shard: [1, 2, 3, 4]

name: Tests (Shard ${{ matrix.shard }}/4)

steps:
  - name: Run tests
    run: pest --parallel --shard ${{ matrix.shard }}/4
```

Type Coverage Is Much Faster
----------------------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/pest-v4-is-here-now-with-browser-testing.md#type-coverage-is-much-faster)

Remember the days when you had to wait for your type coverage to run? Not anymore! Pest v4 introduces a new type coverage engine that is significantly faster than previous versions.

Type coverage is 2x faster on the first run and instant on subsequent runs. This means you can quickly check your type coverage without waiting for long periods, making your development workflow much more efficient.

In addition, Type Coverage now supports **Sharding**. This means you can run type coverage with the `--shard` option, just like you do with your tests.

Profanity Checking
------------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/pest-v4-is-here-now-with-browser-testing.md#profanity-checking)

Pest v4 introduces a new feature that allows you to check for profanity in your test code. This is particularly useful for maintaining a clean and professional codebase, especially in collaborative environments.

You can enable profanity checking by adding the `--profanity` option when running Pest:

```shell
./vendor/bin/pest --profanity
```

To start using Pest's Profanity plugin, you need to require the plugin via Composer.

```shell
composer require pestphp/pest-plugin-profanity --dev
```

After requiring the plugin, you may utilize the `--profanity` option to generate a report of your profanity.

```shell
./vendor/bin/pest --profanity
```

[![](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/raw/4.x/assets/img/profanity.png)](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/assets/img/profanity.png)

If any of your files contain profanity, they will be highlighted in red and displayed using their respective line numbers and the profane word(s) that have been found.

As an example, `pr31(f*ck)` means that the word "fuck" was found on line 31.

To learn more about the Profanity plugin and how to configure it, check out the [Profanity documentation](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/docs/profanity)
.

### Skip Locally or On CI

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/pest-v4-is-here-now-with-browser-testing.md#skip-locally-or-on-ci)

Pest v4 introduces the ability to conditionally skip tests based on the environment. You can use `skipLocally()` to skip tests when running locally, or `skipOnCi` to skip tests when running on a CI server.

```html
it('does not run locally', function () {
    // This test will be skipped when running locally
})->skipLocally();

it('does not run on CI', function () {
    // This test will be skipped when running on a CI server
})->skipOnCi();
```

### Miscellaneous Improvements

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/pest-v4-is-here-now-with-browser-testing.md#miscellaneous-improvements)

*   You may now use `skipLocally()` or `skipOnCi` to conditionally skip tests based on the environment.
*   The `not->toHaveSuspiciousCharacters()` arch expectation has been added to help you identify potential suspicious characters in your code. This arch expectation is now enabled by default on the `php` arch preset. This expectation requires the `intl` PHP extension.
*   The expectation `toBeSlug` has been added to help you validate that a string is a valid slug.

### On Top of PHPUnit 12

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/pest-v4-is-here-now-with-browser-testing.md#on-top-of-phpunit-12)

Pest v4 is built on top of PHPUnit 12, which means you get all the latest features and improvements from PHPUnit. As such, be sure to check out the [PHPUnit 12 release announcement](https://phpunit.de/announcements/phpunit-12.html)
.

### Thanks To You, Pest v4 Is Here!

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/pest-v4-is-here-now-with-browser-testing.md#thanks-to-you-pest-v4-is-here)

There's never been a better time to dive into testing and start using Pest. If you're ready to get started with Pest v4 right away, check out our [installation guide](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/docs/installation)
 for step-by-step instructions. And if you're currently using an earlier version of Pest, we've got you covered with detailed upgrade instructions in our [upgrade guide](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/docs/upgrade-guide)
.

Thank you for your continued support and feedback. We can't wait to see what you build with Pest v4!

* * *

Thank you for reading about Pest v4's new features! Want to get started with Pest? You can find the installation guide in the next section of the documentation: [Installation →](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/docs/installation)

You can’t perform that action at this time.

|     |     |
| --- | --- |
| title | Pest's Spicy Summer Release |
| description | Pest's Spicy Summer release is here - snapshot testing, describe blocks, type coverage, and more... |

Pest's Spicy Summer Release
===========================

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/pest-spicy-summer-release.md#pests-spicy-summer-release)

> "Spicy Summer" is the codename assigned to Pest 2.9.

On March 20, 2023, [we proudly introduced Pest 2.0](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/docs/announcing-pest2)
, marking it as our most significant release to date, with **more than 7 million downloads** at the time of writing. This version showcased a remarkable architectural plugin, an 80% speed improvement in parallel testing, profiling options, and numerous other features.

As we approach summer, we are thrilled to announce our upcoming release: the highly anticipated "Spicy Summer" release. This release brings an array of exciting features that will make it feel like a major version without actually being one - it's Pest v2.9.0 - so **it's just a "composer update" away from you**. Without further delay, let's dive into what we have in store for you this summer:

*   **Built-in Snapshot Testing**, for testing the long-output of your code with ease
*   **Describe Blocks**, for grouping tests and sharing setup and teardown logic
*   **Architectural Testing++**, even more powerful architectural testing
*   **Type Coverage Plugin**, for measuring the percentage of code that is covered by type declarations
*   **Drift Plugin**, to automatically convert your PHPUnit tests to Pest

Built-in Snapshot Testing
-------------------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/pest-spicy-summer-release.md#built-in-snapshot-testing)

> Read the full documentation at: [pestphp.com/docs/snapshot-testing](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/docs/snapshot-testing)

Snapshot testing is a testing technique that allows you to assert that the output of a function or method has not changed. It's a great way to test your codebase and ensure that your code is not changing unexpectedly.

And now, we are proud to announce that Pest will have built-in snapshot testing support. As an example, let's say your "contacts" endpoint outputs a certain HTML every time it runs. You would probably write a test like this:

```html
it('has a contact page', function () {
    $response = $this->get('/contact');

    expect($response)->toMatchSnapshot();
});
```

The first time you run this test, it will create a snapshot file - at `tests/.pest/snapshots` - with the response content. The next time you run the test, it will compare the response with the snapshot file. If the response is different, the test will fail. If the response is the same, the test will pass.

In addition, the given expectation value doesn't have to be a response; it can be anything. For example, you can snapshot an array:

```html
$array = /** Fetch array somewhere */;

expect($array)->toMatchSnapshot();
```

And of course, you can "rebuild" the snapshots at any time by using the `--update-snapshots` option:

```shell
./vendor/bin/pest --update-snapshots
```

Describe Blocks
---------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/pest-spicy-summer-release.md#describe-blocks)

Since we released Pest, describe blocks has been one of the most requested features. These are fundamental to any "functional" testing framework, as they allow you to group tests and share setup and teardown logic.

```html
beforeEach(fn () => $this->user = User::factory()->create());

describe('auth', function () {
    beforeEach(fn () => $this->actingAs($this->user));

    test('cannot login when already logged in', function () {
        // ...
    });

    test('can logout', function () {
        // ...
    });
})->skip(/* Skip the entire describe block */);

describe('guest', function () {
    test('can login', function () {
        // ...
    });
    
    // ...
});
```

Architectural Testing++
-----------------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/pest-spicy-summer-release.md#architectural-testing)

> Read the full documentation at: [pestphp.com/docs/arch-testing](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/docs/arch-testing)

Pest has always been about making testing more enjoyable. Last release, we introduced architectural expectations, which allow you to test your codebase's architecture. This release, we are proud to announce that Pest improves architectural expectations by adding new ones.

```html
test('controllers')
    ->expect('App\Http\Controllers')
    ->toUseStrictTypes()
    ->toHaveSuffix('Controller') // or toHavePreffix, ...
    ->toBeReadonly() 
    ->toBeClasses() // or toBeInterfaces, toBeTraits, ...
    ->classes->not->toBeFinal() // 🌶
    ->classes->toExtendNothing() // or toExtend(Controller::class),
    ->classes->toImplementNothing() // or toImplement(ShouldQueue::class),
```

Type Coverage Plugin
--------------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/pest-spicy-summer-release.md#type-coverage-plugin)

> Read the full documentation at: [pestphp.com/docs/type-coverage](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/docs/type-coverage)

[![](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/raw/4.x/assets/img/type-coverage.png)](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/assets/img/type-coverage.png)

As you may know, Pest offers a `--coverage` flag that allows you to generate a gorgeous coverage report on the terminal. This report shows you which lines of code are covered by your tests. This is a great way to ensure that your tests are covering all of your code.

To add to this, we are proud to announce that Pest will now have built-in type coverage support. This means that you can now see if your source code is using "types" in every possible place. For example, let's say you have a repository that has the following method:

```html
public function find($id)
{
    return User::find($id);
}
```

This method is missing a parameter type and a return type. So, if you run pest --type-coverage, you will see the following output and know that you need to add types to this method:

```shell
...
app/Models\User.php .......................................... 100%
app/Repositories/UserRepository.php .................. pa8, rt8 33%
───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Total: 91.6 %
```

In addition, just like regular coverage, you may enforce `--min` type coverage percentage. For example, if you run `--type-coverage --min=100`, you will see the following output:

```shell
  ...
  app/Models\User.php .......................................................... 100%
  app/Repositories/UserRepository.php .................................. pa8, rt8 33%
  ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
                                                                        Total: 91.6 %
   ERROR  Type coverage below expected: 91.6%. Minimum: 100.0% 
```

Drift Plugin
------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/pest-spicy-summer-release.md#drift-plugin)

> Read the full documentation at: [pestphp.com/docs/migrating-from-phpunit-guide](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/docs/migrating-from-phpunit-guide)

Yes, you read that right. We are proud to announce that Pest will now have a Laravel shift-like tool called Drift. Drift will allow you to upgrade your PHPUnit tests to Pest tests in a matter of seconds.

So, if you have a test like this:

```html
<?php

namespace Tests\Unit;

use PHPUnit\Framework\TestCase;

class ExampleTest extends TestCase
{
    public function test_that_true_is_true(): void
    {
        $this->assertTrue(true);
    }
}
```

You can run `./vendor/bin/pest --drift` and Pest will automatically convert your PHPUnit test to a Pest test:

```html
test('true is true', function () {
    expect(true)->toBeTrue();
});
```

* * *

Thank you for reading about Pest 2.9's new features! If you're considering a testing framework for your next project, here's why you should give Pest a try: [Why Pest →](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/docs/why-pest)

You can’t perform that action at this time.

---

|     |     |
| --- | --- |
| title | Writing Tests |
| description | Next let's get a brief overview of how to write tests using Pest. |

Writing Tests
=============

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/writing-tests.md#writing-tests)

In this section, we will provide a brief overview of how to write tests using Pest. After successfully [installing Pest](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/docs/installation)
, you will find the following files and folders in your project:

    ├── 📂 tests
    │   ├── 📂 Unit
    │   │   └── ExampleTest.php
    │   └── 📂 Feature
    │   │   └── ExampleTest.php
    │   └── TestCase.php
    │   └── Pest.php
    ├── phpunit.xml
    

The `tests` folder serves as the main directory where all your test files will reside. Within this folder, you will find two sub-folders, `Unit` and `Feature`, which house your unit and feature tests, respectively. The `TestCase.php` file is where you can define common functionality or setup that you want to use across all your tests. Lastly, the `Pest.php` file is where you can [configure your test suite](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/docs/configuring-tests)
.

Additionally, a `phpunit.xml` file can be found in the root of your project, and is used to configure PHPUnit's various options when running tests. It's important to note that Pest is built on top of PHPUnit, which means that all the options offered by PHPUnit can also be used in Pest. Therefore, any customization or configuration that you do with the `phpunit.xml` file will also apply to Pest tests.

As you begin writing tests for your project, it's important to consider how to create and organize your test files effectively. Typically, test files are suffixed with `Test.php`, such as `ExampleTest.php`.

Your First Test
---------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/writing-tests.md#your-first-test)

For our first test, let's write something simple. Imagine that your project features a global function called `sum` that adds two numbers together. To test this function, you would create a `Tests\Unit\SumTest.php` file with the following code.

```html
test('sum', function () {
   $result = sum(1, 2);

   expect($result)->toBe(3);
});
```

After writing your test code, it's time to run your tests using Pest. When you execute the `./vendor/bin/pest` command, Pest will display a message indicating whether your tests passed or failed.

[![](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/raw/4.x/assets/img/sum.webp?1)](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/assets/img/sum.webp?1)

As an alternative to the `test()` function, Pest provides the convenient `it()` function that simply prefixes the test description with the word "it", making your tests more readable.

```html
it('performs sums', function () {
   $result = sum(1, 2);

   expect($result)->toBe(3);
});
```

In this case, when you run the `./vendor/bin/pest` command, the output will include the description "it performs sums", along with the result of the test.

[![](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/raw/4.x/assets/img/itsum.webp?1)](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/assets/img/itsum.webp?1)

Finally, you can also use the `describe()` function to group related tests together. For instance, you can use the `describe()` function to group all your tests related to the `sum()` function.

```html
describe('sum', function () {
   it('may sum integers', function () {
       $result = sum(1, 2);

       expect($result)->toBe(3);
    });
   
    it('may sum floats', function () {
       $result = sum(1.5, 2.5);

       expect($result)->toBe(4.0);
    });
});
```

When you run the `./vendor/bin/pest` command, the output will include the description "sum performs sums", along with the result of the test.

Expectation API
---------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/writing-tests.md#expectation-api)

As you may have noticed in our previous examples, we made use of Pest's expectation API to perform assertions in our test code. The `expect()` function is a core part of the expectation API and is used to assert that certain conditions are met.

For instance, in our previous example, we used `expect($result)->toBe(3)` to ensure that the value of `$result` is equal to `3`. Pest's expectation API provides a variety of other assertion functions that you can use to test the behavior of your code, such as `toBeTrue()`, `toBeFalse()`, and `toContain()`.

By using the expectation API, you can write concise and readable assertions that make it clear what your code is doing and how it should behave. In the [next section](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/docs/expectations)
, we will cover some of the most commonly used assertion functions in Pest's expectation API.

Assertion API
-------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/writing-tests.md#assertion-api)

While Pest's expectation API provides a convenient way to perform assertions, it's not the only option available. You can also use PHPUnit's assertion API, which can be useful if you're already familiar with PHPUnit's assertion API or if you need to perform more complex assertions that aren't available in Pest's expectation API.

```html
test('sum', function () {
   $result = sum(1, 2);

   $this->assertSame(3, $result); // Same as expect($result)->toBe(3)
});
```

You can find the full documentation for PHPUnit's assertion API on the PHPUnit website: [docs.phpunit.de/en/11.4/assertions.html](https://docs.phpunit.de/en/11.4/assertions.html)

* * *

Continue to our next section, for more information on how to use the Expectation API: [Expectations →](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/docs/expectations)

You can’t perform that action at this time.

---

### [`‎exceptions.md‎`](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/commit/6f21135cbe8ac6cb28da35f7177ce7a9717c2319#diff-8e8b8ff4c5793efc69088875248571b5bfc1752deaa7ec346232fb10249d7274)

| `72` | `72` | ``   You may also provide a message to the `fail()` method.   `` |
| `73` | `73` | `       ` |
| `74` | `74` | `   ```php   ` |
| `75` |     | `-  it('fail', function () {  ` |
|     | `75` | `+  it('fails', function () {  ` |
| `76` | `76` | `   $this->fail('Something went wrong.');   ` |
| `77` | `77` | `   });   ` |
| `78` | `78` | `   ```   ` |
| `79` | `79` | `       ` |
| `80` |     | ``-  In addition, you can also use the `fails()` method to verify the test fails.  `` |
|     | `80` | ``+  In addition, you can also use the `fails()` method to verify if a test fails.  `` |
| `81` | `81` | `       ` |
| `82` | `82` | `   ```php   ` |
| `83` | `83` | `   it('fails', function () {   ` |
| `84` |     | `-  throw new Exception('Something happened.');  ` |
|     | `84` | `+  $this->fail('Something happened.');  ` |
| `85` | `85` | `   })->fails();   ` |

| `88` |     | ``-  Just like the `fail()` method, you may also provide a message to the `fails()` method.  `` |

Edit and raw actions

|     |     |
| --- | --- |
| title | Team Management |
| description | In this section, we will discuss the process of managing a small team of developers who directly in your Pest test suite. |

Team Management
===============

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/team-management.md#team-management)

With Pest, you can manage tasks and todos with your team directly from the console. You can create, assign, and track tasks, as well as view the status of each task.

Setting Up Project
------------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/team-management.md#setting-up-project)

To get started with team management in Pest, you need to specify the project's URL in your `Pest.php` configuration file. This URL will be used to link todos to the corresponding project management system.

```html
pest()->project()->github('my-organization/my-repository');
```

If you are using a different version control system, you can use the `gitlab`, `bitbucket`, `jira`, or `custom` methods instead.

Creating Todos
--------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/team-management.md#creating-todos)

Typically, todos are linked to one or more tests that need to be passing. As such, tests can be used to track the progress of your todos / tasks. Pest provides a simple way to create todos by using the `todo()` method.

```html
it('has a contact page', function () {
    //
})->todo();
```

When running your tests, Pest will inform you about any tests that are todos so you don't forget and see them in the test results.

[![](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/raw/4.x/assets/img/todo.webp?1)](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/assets/img/todo.webp?1)

If you have one or more todos, you may want to view them separately from the rest of your test suite. You can do this by including the `--todos` option when running Pest.

```shell
./vendor/bin/pest --todos
```

Assigning Todos
---------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/team-management.md#assigning-todos)

In some cases, you may want to assign a todo to a specific team member. Pest allows you to assign a todo to a specific team member by providing their name to the `assignee` argument of the `todo()` method.

```html
it('has a contact page', function () {
    //
})->todo(assignee: 'nunomaduro');
```

You may assign multiple assignees by providing an array of names to the `assignee` argument. Also, you may filter todos by assignee by providing their name to the `--assignee` option when running Pest.

```shell
./vendor/bin/pest --todos --assignee=nunomaduro
```

Set Corresponding Issues
------------------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/team-management.md#set-corresponding-issues)

Sometimes, todos are linked to issues in your project management system. Pest allows you to set the corresponding issue to a todo by providing the issue number to the `issue` argument of the `todo()` method.

```html
it('has a contact page', function () {
    //
})->todo(issue: 123);
```

Just like with assignees, you may set multiple issues by providing an array of issue numbers to the `issue` argument. Also, you may filter todos by issue by providing the issue number to the `--issue` option when running Pest.

```shell
./vendor/bin/pest --todos --issue=123
```

Set Corresponding PRs
---------------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/team-management.md#set-corresponding-prs)

Sometimes, todos are linked to pull requests in your version control system. Pest allows you to set the corresponding pull request to a todo by providing the pull request number to the `pr` argument of the `todo()` method.

```html
it('has a contact page', function () {
    //
})->todo(pr: 123);
```

Just like with assignees, you may set multiple pull requests by providing an array of pull request numbers to the `pr` argument. Also, you may filter todos by pull request by providing the pull request number to the `--pr` option when running Pest.

```shell
./vendor/bin/pest --todos --pr=123
```

Writing Notes for Todos
-----------------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/team-management.md#writing-notes-for-todos)

It is often helpful to provide additional context for a todo. Pest allows you to write notes for a todo by providing a string to the `note` argument of the `todo()` method.

```html
it('has a contact page', function () {
    //
})->todo(note: <<<NOTE
    Given I am a user
    When I visit the contact page
    Then I should see a contact form
NOTE);
```

The notes will be displayed below the todo in the test results.

Marking Todos as Work in Progress
---------------------------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/team-management.md#marking-todos-as-work-in-progress)

Once a todo is completed, you can mark it as work in progress by using the `wip()` method. This method will remove the todo status from the test and mark it as a regular test while keeping all the context like assignees, issues, etc.

```html
it('has a contact page', function () {
    //
})->wip(assignee: 'nunomaduro', issue: 123);
```

Marking Todos as Done
---------------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/team-management.md#marking-todos-as-done)

Once a todo is completed, you can mark it as done by using the `done()` method. This method will remove the todo status from the test and mark it as a regular test while keeping all the context like assignees, issues, etc.

```html
it('has a contact page', function () {
    //
})->done(assignee: 'nunomaduro', issue: 123);
```

Combining Todos with Assignees, Issues, and PRs
-----------------------------------------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/team-management.md#combining-todos-with-assignees-issues-and-prs)

You can combine todos with assignees, issues, and PRs to provide additional context and track the progress of your todos. This can be done using the `describe` group, and the `todo`, `assignee`, `issue`, and `pr` methods.

```html
describe('contacts', function () {
    it('has a contact page', function () {
        //
    }))->issue(123); // or ->pr(123) etc
    
    it('has a contact form', function () {
        //
    })->done(pr: 567);
})->wip(assignee: 'nunomaduro');
```

* * *

Next, we will explore browser testing with Pest, which allows you to test your application's user interface in a real browser environment. This is particularly useful for testing complex interactions and ensuring that your application behaves as expected from a user's perspective: [Browser Testing →](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/docs/browser-testing)

You can’t perform that action at this time.

Browser Testing
===============

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#browser-testing)

Browser testing is an essential part of modern web development, allowing you to ensure that your application works correctly across different browsers and devices. Pest provides a simple and elegant way to write browser tests. Here is an example of how to write a browser test using Pest:

```html
it('may welcome the user', function () {
    $page = visit('/');

    $page->assertSee('Welcome');
});
```

This is a basic example of a browser test that checks if the homepage contains the text "Welcome". However, Pest's browser testing capabilities go beyond this simple example. You can use various methods to interact with the page, such as clicking buttons, filling out forms, and navigating between pages.

Here is an example of a more complex browser test, on Laravel, that checks if a user can sign in:

```html
it('may sign in the user', function () {
    Event::fake();

    User::factory()->create([ // assumes RefreshDatabase trait is used on Pest.php...\
        'email' => 'nuno@laravel.com',\
        'password' => 'password',\
    ]);

    $page = visit('/')->on()->mobile()->firefox();

    $page->click('Sign In')
         ->assertUrlIs('/login')
         ->assertSee('Sign In to Your Account')
         ->fill('email', 'nuno@laravel.com')
         ->fill('password', 'password')
         ->click('Submit')
         ->assertSee('Dashboard');

    $this->assertAuthenticated();

    Event::assertDispatched(UserLoggedIn::class);
});
```

Note that, you are leveraging the full power of Laravel's testing capabilities, such as refresh database, event faking, and authentication assertions, while also actually doing browser testing.

Getting Started
---------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#getting-started)

To get started with browser testing in Pest, you need to install the Pest Browser plugin. You can do this by running the following command:

```shell
composer require pestphp/pest-plugin-browser --dev

npm install playwright@latest
npx playwright install
```

Finally, add `tests/Browser/Screenshots` to your `.gitignore` file to avoid committing screenshots taken during browser tests.

### Running Browser Tests

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#running-browser-tests)

Running browser tests is similar to running regular Pest tests:

```shell
./vendor/bin/pest
```

We recommend running tests in parallel using the `--parallel` option to speed up the execution:

```shell
./vendor/bin/pest --parallel
```

For debugging purposes, you can run the tests in a headed mode and pause the execution at the end of the failed test run:

```shell
./vendor/bin/pest --debug
```

### Navigation

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#navigation)

The `visit()` method is used to navigate to a specific URL in your browser test. It provides various methods to interact with the page:

```html
test('example', function () {
    $page = visit('/');

    $page->assertSee('Welcome');
});
```

### Using Other Browsers

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#using-other-browsers)

By default, the `visit()` method uses Chrome as the browser. However, if you want to use a different browser, you can specify it using the `--browser` option when running the tests:

```shell
./vendor/bin/pest --browser firefox
./vendor/bin/pest --browser safari
```

If you wish to use a different browser by default without specifying it in the command line, you can set it in your `Pest.php` configuration file:

```html
pest()->browser()->inFirefox();
pest()->browser()->inSafari();
```

### Using Other Devices

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#using-other-devices)

The `visit()` method uses a desktop viewport. However, you can specify a mobile viewport using the `onMobile()` method. For example:

```html
$page = visit('/')->on()->mobile();
```

If you wish to use a specific device, you can use the `on()` method and chain it with the `macbook14`, `iPhone14Pro`, etc:

```html
$page = visit('/')->on()->iPhone14Pro();
```

### Using Dark Mode

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#using-dark-mode)

Pest enforces a light color scheme by default. However, you can specify a dark color scheme using the `inDarkMode()` method:

```html
$page = visit('/')->inDarkMode();
```

### Visiting Multiple Pages

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#visiting-multiple-pages)

You can visit multiple pages simultaneously by passing an array of URLs to the `visit()` method. This is useful for testing scenarios where you need to interact with multiple pages at once:

```html
$pages = visit(['/', '/about']);

$pages->assertNoSmoke()
    ->assertNoAccessibilityIssues()
    ->assertNoConsoleLogs()
    ->assertNoJavaScriptErrors();

[$homePage, $aboutPage] = $pages;

$homePage->assertSee('Welcome to our website');
$aboutPage->assertSee('About Us');
```

### Navigation

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#navigation-1)

After visiting a page, you can navigate to other pages using the `navigate()` method. This method allows you to navigate to a different URL while keeping the current browser context:

```html
$page = visit('/');

$page->navigate('/about')
     ->assertSee('About Us');
```

### Locating Elements

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#locating-elements)

You can locate elements in the DOM using text or CSS selectors. Pest provides a simple syntax for locating elements:

```html
// Clicks the first link with the text "Login"
$page->click('Login');

// Clicks the first element with the class "btn-primary"
$page->click('.btn-primary');

// Clicks the element with the data-test attribute "login"
$page->click('@login');

// Clicks the element with the ID "submit-button"
$page->click('#submit-button');

// etc...
```

### Configuring Timeouts

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#configuring-timeouts)

Sometimes, elements may take time to appear on the page. By default, Pest waits for `5` seconds before timing out. You can configure the default timeout for browser tests in your `Pest.php` configuration file:

```html
pest()->browser()->timeout(10000);
```

### Configuring User Agent

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#configuring-user-agent)

By default, the User Agent will default to the Browser you're running for tests such as: `Mozilla/5.0 (Windows NT 10.0; Win64; x64) AppleWebKit/537.36 (KHTML, like Gecko) HeadlessChrome/133.0.6943.16 Safari/537.36`

You may wish to override the User Agent of the browser for all of your tests, you can configure this in the `Pest.php` configuration file:

```html
pest()->browser()->userAgent('CustomUserAgent');
```

### Configuring Host

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#configuring-host)

By default, the server will bind to `127.0.0.1` for all browser tests.

You may wish to override the host for subdomain applications. You can configure this in the `Pest.php` configuration file:

```html
pest()->browser()->withHost('some-subdomain.localhost');
```

### Geolocation

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#geolocation)

Sometimes, you need to define where the browser believes it is physically on the earth. This method takes a latitude and longitude and will set the `geolocation` permission in the browser and then make the coordinates available via Javascript's getCurrentPosition API:

```html
$page = visit('/')
     ->geolocation(39.399872, -8.224454);
```

### Configuring Locale

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#configuring-locale)

You can set the locale for your test requests using the `withLocale` method. This is particularly useful for testing multilingual applications.

```html
$page = visit('/')->withLocale('fr-FR');

$page->assertSee('Bienvenue');
```

### Configuring Timezone

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#configuring-timezone)

You can set the timezone for your test requests using the `withTimezone` method. This is useful for testing date and time displays in different time zones.

```html
$page = visit('/')->withTimezone('America/New_York');

$page->assertSee('EST');
```

### Configuring UserAgent

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#configuring-useragent)

You can set the User-Agent header for your test requests using the `withUserAgent` method. This is useful for testing how your application responds to different types of clients, such as mobile browsers or bots.

```html
$page = visit('/')->withUserAgent('Googlebot');

$page->assertSee('Welcome, bot!');
```

### Configuring Host

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#configuring-host-1)

You can set the host for your test server using the `withHost` method. This is useful for testing subdomains or where different hosts serve different content.

```html
$page = visit('/dashboard')->withHost('some-subdomain.localhost');

$page->assertSee('Welcome to Some Subdomain');
```

Element Assertions
------------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#element-assertions)

### assertTitle

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#asserttitle)

The `assertTitle` method asserts that the page title matches the given text:

```html
$page->assertTitle('Home Page');
```

### assertTitleContains

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#asserttitlecontains)

The `assertTitleContains` method asserts that the page title contains the given text:

```html
$page->assertTitleContains('Home');
```

### assertSee

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#assertsee)

The `assertSee` method asserts that the given text is present on the page:

```html
$page->assertSee('Welcome to our website');
```

### assertDontSee

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#assertdontsee)

The `assertDontSee` method asserts that the given text is not present on the page:

```html
$page->assertDontSee('Error occurred');
```

### assertSeeIn

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#assertseein)

The `assertSeeIn` method asserts that the given text is present within the selector:

```html
$page->assertSeeIn('.header', 'Welcome');
```

### assertDontSeeIn

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#assertdontseein)

The `assertDontSeeIn` method asserts that the given text is not present within the selector:

```html
$page->assertDontSeeIn('.error-container', 'Error occurred');
```

### assertSeeAnythingIn

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#assertseeanythingin)

The `assertSeeAnythingIn` method asserts that any text is present within the selector:

```html
$page->assertSeeAnythingIn('.content');
```

### assertSeeNothingIn

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#assertseenothingin)

The `assertSeeNothingIn` method asserts that no text is present within the selector:

```html
$page->assertSeeNothingIn('.empty-container');
```

### assertCount

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#assertcount)

The `assertCount` method asserts that a given element is present a given amount of times:

```html
$page->assertCount('.item', 5);
```

### assertScript

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#assertscript)

The `assertScript` method asserts that the given JavaScript expression evaluates to the given value:

```html
$page->assertScript('document.title', 'Home Page');
$page->assertScript('document.querySelector(".btn").disabled', true);
```

### assertSourceHas

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#assertsourcehas)

The `assertSourceHas` method asserts that the given source code is present on the page:

```html
$page->assertSourceHas('<h1>Welcome</h1>');
```

### assertSourceMissing

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#assertsourcemissing)

The `assertSourceMissing` method asserts that the given source code is not present on the page:

```html
$page->assertSourceMissing('<div class="error">');
```

### assertSeeLink

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#assertseelink)

The `assertSeeLink` method asserts that the given link is present on the page:

```html
$page->assertSeeLink('About Us');
```

### assertDontSeeLink

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#assertdontseelink)

The `assertDontSeeLink` method asserts that the given link is not present on the page:

```html
$page->assertDontSeeLink('Admin Panel');
```

### assertChecked

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#assertchecked)

The `assertChecked` method asserts that the given checkbox is checked:

```html
$page->assertChecked('terms');
$page->assertChecked('color', 'blue'); // For checkbox with specific value
```

### assertNotChecked

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#assertnotchecked)

```html

```

### assertIndeterminate

### assertRadioSelected

### assertValue

### assertValueIsNot

### assertAttribute

### assertAttributeMissing

### assertAttributeContains

Console Assertions
------------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#console-assertions)

### assertNoSmoke

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#assertnosmoke)

The `assertNoSmoke` method asserts there are no console logs or JavaScript errors on the page:

```html
$page->assertNoSmoke();
```

### assertNoConsoleLogs

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#assertnoconsolelogs)

The `assertNoConsoleLogs` method asserts there are no console logs on the page:

```html
$page->assertNoConsoleLogs();
```

### assertNoJavaScriptErrors

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#assertnojavascripterrors)

The `assertNoJavaScriptErrors` method asserts there are no JavaScript errors on the page:

```html
$page->assertNoJavaScriptErrors();
```

### assertNoAccessibilityIssues

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#assertnoaccessibilityissues)

The `assertNoAccessibilityIssues` method asserts there are no "serious" accessibility issues on the page:

```html
$page->assertNoAccessibilityIssues();
```

By default, the level is 1 (serious). You can change to one of the following levels:

    0. Critical
    1. Serious
    2. Moderate
    3. Minor
    

*   The level 0 (critical) only reports issues that cause severe barriers for individuals with disabilities. The organization may be subject to legal action if these issues are not addressed.
*   The level 1 (serious) includes all critical issues (level 0) and adds issues that significantly impact accessibility. The organization may be subject to legal action if these issues are not addressed.
*   The level 2 (moderate) includes all serious issues (level 1) and adds issues that moderately affect accessibility. The end-user would appreciate the fix, but it is not a barrier.
*   The level 3 (minor) includes all moderate issues (level 2) and adds issues that have a minor impact on accessibility. These issues are often related to best practices and do not significantly affect the user experience.

Screenshot Assertions
---------------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#screenshot-assertions)

### assertScreenshotMatches

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#assertscreenshotmatches)

The `assertScreenshotMatches` method asserts that the screenshot matches the expected image:

```html
$page->assertScreenshotMatches();
$page->assertScreenshotMatches(true, true); // Full page, show diff
```

Element Interactions
--------------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#element-interactions-1)

### click

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#click)

The `click` method clicks the link with the given text:

```html
$page->click('Login');
```

You may also pass options:

```html
$page->click('#button', options: ['clickCount' => 2]);
```

### text

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#text)

The `text` method gets the text of the element matching the given selector:

```html
$text = $page->text('.header');
```

### attribute

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#attribute)

The `attribute` method gets the given attribute from the element matching the given selector:

```html
$alt = $page->attribute('img', 'alt');
```

### keys

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#keys)

The `keys` method sends the given keys to the element matching the given selector:

```html
$page->keys('input[name=password]', 'secret');
$page->keys('input[name=password]', ['{Control}', 'a']); // Keyboard shortcuts
```

### withKeyDown

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#withkeydown)

The `withKeyDown` method executes the given callback while a key is held down:

```html
$page->withKeyDown('Shift', function () use ($page): void {
    $page->keys('#input', ['KeyA', 'KeyB', 'KeyC']);
}); // writes "ABC"
```

> Note: To respect held keys like Shift, use key codes such as KeyA, KeyB, KeyC. 'a' always types a lowercase “a” and 'A' always types an uppercase “A”, regardless of modifiers.

### type

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#type)

The `type` method types the given value in the given field:

```html
$page->type('email', 'test@example.com');
```

### typeSlowly

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#typeslowly)

The `typeSlowly` method types the given value in the given field slowly, like a user:

```html
$page->typeSlowly('email', 'test@example.com');
```

### select

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#select)

The `select` method selects the given value in the given field:

```html
$page->select('country', 'US');
$page->select('interests', ['music', 'sports']); // Multiple select
```

### append

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#append)

The `append` method types the given value in the given field without clearing it:

```html
$page->append('description', ' Additional information.');
```

### clear

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#clear)

The `clear` method clears the given field:

```html
$page->clear('search');
```

### radio

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#radio)

The `radio` method selects the given value of a radio button field:

```html
$page->radio('size', 'large');
```

### check

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#check)

The `check` method checks the given checkbox:

```html
$page->check('terms');
$page->check('color', 'blue'); // For checkbox with specific value
```

### uncheck

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#uncheck)

The `uncheck` method unchecks the given checkbox:

```html
$page->uncheck('newsletter');
$page->uncheck('color', 'red'); // For checkbox with specific value
```

### attach

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#attach)

The `attach` method attaches the given file to the field:

```html
$page->attach('avatar', '/path/to/image.jpg');
```

### press

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#press)

The `press` method presses the button with the given text or name:

```html
$page->press('Submit');
```

### pressAndWaitFor

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#pressandwaitfor)

The `pressAndWaitFor` method presses the button with the given text or name and waits for a specified amount of time:

```html
$page->pressAndWaitFor('Submit', 2); // Wait for 2 seconds
```

### drag

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#drag)

The `drag` method drags an element to another element using selectors:

```html
$page->drag('#item', '#target');
```

### hover

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#hover)

The `hover` method hovers over the given element:

```html
$page->hover('#item');
```

### submit

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#submit)

The `submit` method submits the first form found on the page:

```html
$page->submit();
```

### value

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#value)

The `value` method gets the value of the element matching the given selector:

```html
$value = $page->value('input[name=email]');
```

### withinIframe

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#withiniframe)

The `withinIframe` method allows you to interact with elements inside an iframe:

```html
use Pest\Browser\Api\PendingAwaitablePage;

$page->withinIframe('.iframe-container', function (PendingAwaitablePage $page) {
    $page->type('frame-input', 'Hello iframe')
        ->click('frame-button');
});
```

### resize

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#resize)

You may use the resize method to adjust the size of the browser window:

```html
$page->resize(1280, 720);
```

### script

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#script)

The `script` method executes a script in the context of the page:

```html
$result = $page->script('document.title');
```

### content

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#content)

The `content` method gets the page's content:

```html
$html = $page->content();
```

### url

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#url)

The `url` method gets the page's URL:

```html
$currentUrl = $page->url();
```

### wait

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#wait)

The `wait` method pauses for the given number of seconds:

```html
$page->wait(2); // Wait for 2 seconds
```

### waitForKey

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#waitforkey)

The `waitForKey` method opens the current page URL in the default web browser and waits for a key press:

```html
$page->waitForKey(); // Useful for debugging
```

Debugging tests
---------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#debugging-tests-1)

Sometimes you may want to debug your browser tests. Pest provides a convenient way to do this by using the `--debug` option, which makes pest to open the browser window and pause the execution of the test when it fails. You can then inspect the page and see what went wrong.

```shell
./vendor/bin/pest --debug
```

Optionally, you can also use the `debug()` method in your test. It will limit execution to this test (like using [`only()`](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/filtering-tests.md#only)
), pause the execution and open the browser window:

```html
$page->debug();
```

You can also take a screenshot of the current page using the `screenshot()` method. This is useful for visual debugging:

NOTE: If you don't pass the filename, it will use the test name as the filename.

```html
$page->screenshot();
$page->screenshot(fullPage: true);
$page->screenshot(filename: 'custom-name');
```

You can also take a screenshot of a specific element using the `screenshotElement()` method:

```html
$page->screenshotElement('#my-element');
```

You can also use the `tinker()` method to open a Tinker session in the context of the current page. This allows you to interact with the page using PHP code:

```html
$page->tinker();
```

After you can run your tests with the `--headed` option to open the browser window:

```shell
./vendor/bin/pest --headed
```

If you wish to run the tests in a headed mode by default, you can set it in your `Pest.php` configuration file:

```html
pest()->browser()->headed();
```

Continuous Integration
----------------------

[](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/browser-testing.md#continuous-integration)

You may refer to Pest's [Continuous Integration](https://pestphp.com/docs/continuous-integration)
 documentation for more information on how to run your browser tests in a CI environment.

However, if you are using GitHub Actions, you need to add the following steps to your workflow file:

```yaml
    - uses: actions/setup-node@v4
      with:
        node-version: lts/*

    - name: Install dependencies
      run: npm ci

    - name: Install Playwright Browsers
      run: npx playwright install --with-deps
```

* * *

Now, let's dive into architectural testing and how it can benefit your development process. By performing architectural testing, you can evaluate the overall design of your application and identify potential flaws before they become significant issues: [Arch Testing](https://github.com/pestphp/docs/blob/4.x/docs/arch-testing)

You can’t perform that action at this time.

| `12` | `12` | `   **The first step** is to require Pest as a "dev" dependency in your project by running the following commands on your command line.   ` |
